                            <div class="player-info-box-header team-giants"><div class="player-info-box-name"><h1>Andrew McCutchen</h1><div class="player-info-box-name-team"><a href="/teams/giants">San Francisco Giants</a></div></div><div class="player-info-box-item">Age: 31</div><div class="player-info-box-item">Bats/Throws: R/R</div>
        <div class="player-info-box-item">5' 10" / 195</div>
        <div class="player-info-box-pos">OF</div></div>
                        <div class="player-info-bio">
                            <strong>Birthdate: </strong>10/10/1986 (31 y, 5 m)<br /><b>Drafted:</b> <a href="statss.aspx?playerid=9847&position=OF#draft" style="text-decoration:none;">2005 June Amateur Draft - Round: 1, Pick: 11, Overall: 11, Team: Pittsburgh Pirates</a><br /><strong>Contract:</strong> <a href="statss.aspx?playerid=9847&position=OF#contract" >$51.5M / 6 Years (2012 - 2017) + 1 Option Years</a>
                        </div>
                    </td>

                    
                    <tr><td><hr class="player-page-info-sep"/><div class="player-page-rotowire"><strong><a href="https://www.rotowire.com/users/ad_jump.asp?id=688&playerid=8626">RotoWire News</a>:</strong> McCutchen, who was acquired by the Giants on Monday via trade, was told he'll play a corner outfield spot for his new club in 2018, Buster Olney of ESPN reports. (1/16/2018)</div></td></tr>

        <td style="width: 302px; height: 250px; vertical-align: top;">
            <div class="catchall300" style='width:300px; overflow:hidden;float:right;'><!-- RoS_300x250 --> <div id ='div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13' style='width:300px; height:250px; overflow:hidden;'><script type='text/javascript'>if ($('#div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13').is(':visible')) {googletag.cmd.push(function () { googletag.display('div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13'); });}</script></div></div>

    <tr>
        
        <tr id="so2" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Year in Review: </b>The 11th-overall pick in the 2005 draft began the season at Triple-A Indianapolis, showing unprecedented power with a .303/.361/.493 line in 219 plate appearances. McCutchen reached Pittsburgh in June, taking over center field following the Nate McLouth trade. No adjustment time was needed: McCutchen quickly showed off his wide array of tools. The 5’11’’ speedster posted a .368 wOBA, driving the ball with surprising force. McCutchen had a .185 ISO, popping 12 homers and notching nine triples. He took the plate approach of a seasoned veteran, offering at only 21% of pitches thrown out of the zone and walking in 11% of his plate appearances. McCutchen used his sizzling speed to swipe 22 bases in 27 attempts. Pitchers hoping to zip a fastball past the rookie paid dearly, as McCutchen hammered heaters for +1.5 runs above average per 100 pitches thrown.<br /><br /><b>The Year Ahead: </b>Just 23 years old entering the 2010 season, McCutchen has the skills to be a fantasy monster. He is one of the fastest players in the Majors, works the count well, and possesses more sock than one would expect given his 175 pound frame. It might be wise, however, to expect a little less power from McCutchen next season: his career minor league ISO is .137. While it's hard to find faults in a five-tool player, McCutchen is still learning how to hit breaking stuff. He was -0.8 runs below average per 100 pitches against sliders, and a full two runs below average against curveballs. However, fantasy owners shouldn't hesitate in the slightest to lay down a high draft pick on Pittsburgh's franchise player. McCutchen's blend of speed, patience, and power is extremely rare. This kind of across-the-board production wins championships.  (David Golebiewski)</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so3" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Pittsburgh's franchise player proved his cross-category prowess in 2010, working the count, using his wheels and adding a dash of power for good measure. McCutchen batted .286/.365/.449, with a .363 wOBA that matched up pretty well with his .368 mark during his rookie season in 2009. The 11th-overall selection in the '05 draft stole 33 bases in 43 attempts (a 77% success rate), but he offered more than base thievery. He displayed superb strike-zone discipline by swinging at just 20% of pitches thrown out of the zone. The MLB average was 29.3%, and McCutchen's O-Swing was lowest in the National League among qualified hitters. Putting pitchers in tough counts (McCutchen's 56.4 first pitch strike percentage was below the 58.8% MLB average), he walked 10.7% of the time. And the quick-wristed center fielder popped 16 HR with a .163 ISO. McCutchen is already a fantasy star, and considering that he'll play the entire 2011 season at age 24, we likely haven't seen his best yet.  (David Golebiewski)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Few players in the game offer McCutchen's blend of speed, power, patience and upside. Draft him high and enjoy his entrance into full-fledged superstardom. </td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so4" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>While his batting average dropped, 'Cutch turned in his best offensive season to date by bumping up his walk rate and using his whip-quick wrists to hit for more power. McCutchen drew ball four a career-high 13.1 percent of the time and cracked 23 home runs, besting his 2010 total by seven. The Bucs' center fielder is on the small side (5-foot-10, 190 pounds), but went deep more often by decreasing his ground ball rate from 43 to 38 percent and not hitting as many pop ups (six percent of his batted balls, compared to nine percent the previous two years). About the only thing he didn't improve upon was baserunning, as his 23 steals and 70 percent success rate were a bit disappointing. Even so, he was a down-ballot MVP candidate at age 24, and it will only get better from here. (David Golebiewski)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>If everything clicks, McCutchen has the power/speed combo to join Barry Bonds as the second Pirate ever to post a 30/30 season. He's already close to being a perennial first-round pick.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so5" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Andrew McCutchen was very good from 2009 to 2011, but he stepped it up a notch in 2012. McCutchen posted all-world offensive numbers, hitting 31 homers and stealing 20 bags, all while maintaining a .327 batting average. The jump in power production is a tad surprising since the right-hander hit more balls on the ground in 2012 than ever before, but another year of physical maturation could result in the 26-year-old maintaining his numbers. Odds are McCutchen’s batting average will fall, as even he isn’t good enough to sustain a .375 batting average on balls in play year-after-year. If you want McCutchen on your 2013 roster, you’re going to have to take him in the first round, and since he doesn't steal elite-level bags, and that batting average will likely regress, he may be a tad over-rated. (Zach Sanders)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Andrew McCutchen has turned himself into an elite fantasy outfielder, so if you want him on your 2013 roster, you’ll have to take him in the first round.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so6" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Given how excellent he is, it's tough to be hard on Andrew McCutchen. But fantasy baseball managers are tough on their players, especially their elite, first-round, big-investment stars. So where are the faults? Well, Cutch took a step back in power in 2013 -- his homer total (21) and isolated slugging percentage (.190) moved towards his early career levels. While his batted ball distance was good (27th in baseball, 297 feet on average), his home run per fly ball number was not great (12.4%, 10.5% was league average). The Bucs' center fielder also doesn't steal an elite number of bases -- his 27 from last year was the best in the last three years, so he could be projected to regress from that level. But now it's time to say something nice. If you add homers and stolen bags together for a crude measure of power and speed, McCutchen was 11th in baseball, and one of four in the top fifteen to pair that ability with a good batting average. The other guys? Mike Trout, Miguel Cabrera and Paul Goldschmidt. Heady company. Even if you step back the steals some, McCutchen is only 27 and could add power to offset that loss. And, considering that his worst season since his rookie year still had him hit .259 with 23 homers and 23 steals, it seems his floor is very high. (<a href="http://www.twitter.com/enosarris">Eno Sarris</a>)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Maybe Andrew McCutchen won't hit enough homers and steal enough bases to be a top-three fantasy player in 2014. That's fine. His floor is so high that a strong investment in him is a safe one. At 27, there's no reason to worry yet.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so7" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>It’s difficult to poke holes in Andrew McCutchen’s game. After a “down” year — only by his own incredible standards — in 2013 in terms of power, McCutchen was well on his way to another season like 2012 last year before a side injury cut his season a little bit short. Still, the worst McCutchen has done in the standard roto categories over the last three seasons are a .314 average, 21 home runs, 83 RBI, 89 runs, and 18 steals. That sounds like a top three pick to me. The only real question is whether McCutchen is the better fantasy option than Giancarlo Stanton for the second spot overall. Given that Stanton has hit 37 home runs in two of his last three seasons, which is probably 10 more than one can safely expect from McCutchen this season, Stanton likely has the edge. But it’s certainly up for debate. (Scott Spratt)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>McCutchen does it all. He hits for average, hits home runs, steals bases, and does so year after year. He will likely be the number three overall pick in most fantasy formats in 2015, and his consistency makes a compelling case for the number two spot.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so8" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Well, it finally happened: Andrew McCutchen didn't pay back his draft price. It's hard to confirm whether last season marked the onset of the slow decline of a generational athlete or was merely a blip on the radar. According to PITCHf/x, Cutch scaled back his already sterling chase rate -- a positive development in light of pitchers more frequently avoiding the zone against him. But his overall contact bottomed out in 2015, losing ground both in and out of the zone, and it's hard to tell yet if it's statistical noise or something worse. McCutchen remains a top-tier outfielder who generates excellent value through volume due to durability and consistency, but there's a high probability he doesn't steal double-digit bases in 2016. That makes him no longer the five-category stud he once was, and as his speed wanes, so, too, will the batting average on balls in play. The floor remains high, and sometimes it's worth paying a premium for safety. But as his ceiling falls, McCutchen distances himself from being a lock for top-10 value at his position, let alone overall. A first-round investment in him, especially in light of the glut of young and emerging talent in the league, would be tenuous. (Alex Chamberlain)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Entering his age-30 season, Cutch's days of top-10 value may be in the rear-view mirror as his stolen base production tapers off. His durability, consistent production and high offensive floor still make him one of 2016's more stable early-round investments, but he'll need to turn back the clock to justify a first-round pick.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so9" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>McCutchen is coming off his worst season by a wide measure. Part of that was a career-worst -18.7 fielding rating. The claim is that he played too shallow. To be this negative, it means he failed to steal singles - the whole point of playing shallow. If so, why didn't the Pirates re-position him? Probably because the "too shallow" argument is a non-sequitur. McCutchen hasn't passed the smell test as an above average center fielder for years. Meanwhile, he's flanked by Starling Marte and Gregory Polanco - two superior defenders. It was past time for McCutchen to move to an outfield corner. The once-great slugger declined at the plate too. The cracks that appeared during his 2015 campaign fissured into serious issues. The most glaring decline was in his typically high batting average on balls in play. Teams figured it out - McCutchen is shiftable. They ran 149 traditional shifts, during which he was only 74% as good as the league average according to weighted runs creatd. He had never been shifted more than 74 times in a season prior to 2016. Expect more shifts against the pull-happy righty. On the plus side, he has enough athleticism to intentionally defeat the shift. It's something to watch, but fantasy owners will certainly have to take on some risk if they roll the dice on him. (Brad Johnson)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>McCutchen was a disaster on defense last year, and his merely average offense was a massive let down. His career began with seven Hall of Fame worthy seasons. We'll see if he can make adjustments and recover the HOF pace in 2017.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
    </tr>

Teams figured it out - McCutchen is shiftable. They ran 149 traditional shifts, during which he was only 74% as good as the league average according to weighted runs creatd. He had never been shifted more than 74 times in a season prior to 2016. Expect more shifts against the pull-happy righty.
